   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of books banned by governments
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=Banned_book&amp;redirect=no" title="Banned book">
       Banned book
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <p>
      <b>
       Banned books
      </b>
      are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Books" title="Books">
       books
      </a>
      to which free access is not permitted. The practice of banning books is a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">
       censorship
      </a>
      , from political, religious, moral, or (less often) commercial motives. This page intends to list alphabetically all known banned books, giving a brief context for each.
     </p>
     <p>
      Such a large number of banned books has led publishers becoming specialized in them. The best-known examples are the Parisian
      <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_Press" title="Obelisk Press">
       Obelisk Press
      </a>
      , which published
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Miller" title="Henry Miller">
       Henry Miller
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer_(novel)" title="Tropic of Cancer (novel)">
        Tropic of Cancer
       </a>
      </i>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Olympia_Press" title="Olympia Press">
       Olympia Press
      </a>
      , which published
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Burroughs" title="William Burroughs">
       William Burroughs
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Naked_Lunch" title="Naked Lunch">
        Naked Lunch
       </a>
      </i>
      . Both of these, the work of father
      <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kahane" title="Jack Kahane">
       Jack Kahane
      </a>
      and son
      <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Girodias" title="Maurice Girodias">
       Maurice Girodias
      </a>
      , specialized in English-language books which were prohibited, at the time, in Great Britain and the United States.
      <a class="extiw" href="//es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruedo_ib%C3%A9rico" title="es:Ruedo ibrico">
       Ruedo Ibrico
      </a>
      , also located in Paris, specialized in books prohibited in Spain during the dictatorship of
      <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
       Francisco Franco
      </a>
      . Russian literature prohibited during the Soviet period was published outside of Russia.
     </p>
     <p>
      Books are still banned today. Nowhere can everything be published, although the prohibitions vary strikingly from one country to another:
      <a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">
       hate speech
      </a>
      , for example, is prohibited in several countries, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_Sweden" title="Censorship in Sweden">
       Sweden
      </a>
      , though legal in the United States, where the only prohibition is on
      <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">
       child pornography
      </a>
      . Some believe that the banning of specific books is appropriate, such as the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protocols_of_the_Elders_of_Zion" title="Protocols of the Elders of Zion">
        Protocols of the Elders of Zion
       </a>
      </i>
      , in Russia, or Hitler's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">
        Mein Kampf
       </a>
      </i>
      , in Austria.
     </p>
     <p>
      At the local level, books have been and still are banned by schools and public libraries. This is usually the result of complaints from parents, who find particular books not appropriate for their children. In many libraries, including the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">
       British Library
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
       Library of Congress
      </a>
      , erotic books are housed in separate collections which require special application.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Libraries sometimes avoid purchasing controversial books, and the personal opinions of librarians have at times impacted book selection.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

       </td>

         Lewis Carroll
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        Children's novel/adventure
       </td>
       <td>
        Formerly banned in the province of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunan,_China" title="Hunan, China">
         Hunan, China
        </a>
        , beginning in 1931, for its portrayal of
        <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">
         anthropomorphized
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animals" title="Animals">
         animals
        </a>
        acting on the same level of complexity as
        <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">
         human
        </a>
        beings. The censor General Ho Chien believed that attributing human language to animals was an insult to humans. He feared that the book would teach children to regard humans and animals on the same level, which would be "disastrous".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-3">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          3
          <span>

          </span>

        <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">

          </span>

          <span>

          <span>
           [
          </span>
          10
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">
         Islamic
        </a>
        values, most notably the occurrence of an anthropomorphic, talking pig.

          <span>
           [
          </span>
          11
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>

          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        including North Korea.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
         <a href="#cite_note-15">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          15
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        Sometimes, the ban is on distributing the Bible in certain languages or versions. The Bible in Spanish was prohibited in Spain from the sixteenth until the nineteenth century.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
         <a href="#cite_note-16">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          16
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        In 1234, King
        <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">
         James I of Aragon
        </a>
        ordered the burning of Bibles in the vernacular.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
         <a href="#cite_note-17">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          17
          <span>
           ]
          </span>

        Banned in Boston, Massachusetts, Kansas City, Missouri, Camden, New Jersey and other U.S. cities and this novel by Sinclair deals with fanatical religiosity and hypocrisy in the United States during the 1920s by presenting a skeevy preacher (the Reverend Dr. Elmer Gantry) as a protagonist who prefers easy money, booze, and "enticing young girls" over saving souls, all while converting a traveling tent revival crusade into a profitable and permanent evangelical church and radio empire for his employers.

       <td>
        <i>
         Feast for the Seaweeds
        </i>
        (1983)
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Haidar_Haidar" title="Haidar Haidar">
         Haidar Haidar
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        Novel
       </td>
       <td>
        Banned in Egypt and several other Arab states, and even resulted in a belated angry reaction from the clerics of Al-Azhar University upon reprinting in Egypt in the year 2000. The clerics issued a
        <a href="/wiki/Fatwa" title="Fatwa">
         Fatwa
        </a>
        banning the novel, and accused Haidar of heresy and offending Islam.
        <a href="/wiki/Al-Azhar_University" title="Al-Azhar University">
         Al-Azhar University

         </a>
        </i>

       </td>
       <td>

         Adolf Hitler
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        Political manifesto
       </td>
       <td>
        Banned in some European nations and the Russian Federation as extremist.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
         <a href="#cite_note-73">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          73
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <p>
         In Germany, the copyright of the book is claimed by the Free State of
         <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">
          Bavaria
         </a>
         and Bavarian authorities try to prevent any reprinting. It is legal to own or distribute existing copies.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
          <a href="#cite_note-74">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           74
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </p>
        <p>
         In Austria, the
         <a href="/wiki/Verbotsgesetz_1947" title="Verbotsgesetz 1947">
          Verbotsgesetz 1947
         </a>
         prohibits the printing of the book. It is illegal to own or distribute existing copies.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
          <a href="#cite_note-75">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           75
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         The law ( 3 d.) states that, "Whoever publicly or before several people, through the printing of disseminated writings or illustrations to one of under  1 or  3 prohibited acts requests, strives or seeks to induce others, especially for the purpose of glorifying or advertising the aims of the Nazi Party, its institutions or measures, provided that it does not constitute a serious criminal offense, will be punished with imprisonment from five to ten years, or up to twenty years for offenders who themselves or their actions are deemed especially dangerous."
        </p>
       </td>

      <tr>
       <td>
        <i>
         The Meritorious Price of Our Redemption
        </i>
        (1650)
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/William_Pynchon" title="William Pynchon">
         William Pynchon
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        Religious critique
       </td>
       <td>
        The first book banned in the
        <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
         New World
        </a>
        . Pynchon, a prominent leader of the
        <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">
         Massachusetts Bay Colony
        </a>
        who, in 1636, founded the City of
        <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">
         Springfield, Massachusetts
        </a>
        , wrote this explicit critique of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritanism" title="Puritanism">
         Puritanism
        </a>
        , published in London in 1650. That year, several copies made their way back to the New World. Pynchon, who resided in Springfield, was unaware that his book suffered the New World's first book burning, on the
        <a href="/wiki/Boston_Common" title="Boston Common">
         Boston Common
        </a>
        . Accused of
        <a href="/wiki/Heresy" title="Heresy">
         heresy
        </a>
        by the
        <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Court" title="Massachusetts General Court">
         Massachusetts General Court
        </a>
        , Pynchon quietly transferred ownership of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connecticut_River_Valley" title="Connecticut River Valley">
         Connecticut River Valley
        </a>
        's largest land-holdings to his son, and then suffered indignities as he left the New World for England. It was the first work
        <a href="/wiki/Banned_in_Boston" title="Banned in Boston">
         banned in Boston
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
         <a href="#cite_note-76">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          76
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>

       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Perrault" title="Gilles Perrault">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Hassan_II_of_Morocco" title="Hassan II of Morocco">

        </a>

       <td>

       <td>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Polsko-angielsko-niemiecki_Glosariusz_regionalny_Wojew%C3%B3dztwa_Opolskiego" title="Polsko-angielsko-niemiecki Glosariusz regionalny Wojewdztwa Opolskiego">
          Polsko-angielsko-niemiecki Glosariusz regionalny Wojewdztwa Opolskiego

          <span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        (The Polish-English-German Glossary of the Regional Terminology of the Province of Opole) (2004)
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Tomasz_Kamusella" title="Tomasz Kamusella">
         Tomasz Kamusella
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        Reference work
       </td>
       <td>
        Its run of 2000 copies was destroyed on the order of the Self-Governmental Regional Authority (
        <i>
         Urzd Marszakowski
        </i>
        ) of the
        <a href="/wiki/Opole_Voivodeship" title="Opole Voivodeship">
         Province of Opole
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
         Poland
        </a>
        , because in the overview of the history of the region the reference, apart from giving the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" title="People's Republic of Poland">
         Polish
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
         Soviet
        </a>
        view according to which the new
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oder-Neisse_line" title="Oder-Neisse line">
         Polish-German border
        </a>
        was recognized in 1945 at the
        <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">
         Potsdam Conference
        </a>
        , also included the view propounded by the
        <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
         Western Allies
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">
         West Germany
        </a>
        , namely, that the border was finally and fully recognized in light of international law only when the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German-Polish_Border_Treaty_(1990)" title="German-Polish Border Treaty (1990)">
         German-Polish Border Treaty (1990)
        </a>
        was ratified in 1992. Deputy President
        <a href="/wiki/Ryszard_Galla" title="Ryszard Galla">
         Ryszard Galla
        </a>
        publically appealed for
        <a href="/wiki/Book_burning" title="Book burning">
         burning all the copies
        </a>
        of the glossary.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
         <a href="#cite_note-96">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          96
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        The regional authority also ordered the
        <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Poland" title="National Library of Poland">
         National Library of Poland
        </a>
        not to lend its two copies of the reference.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
         <a href="#cite_note-97">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          97
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        The library made them accessible to readers only in 2012, after the regional authority, shamed by the press, withdrew this extrajudicial ban.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
         <a href="#cite_note-98">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          98
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>

        Religious text
       </td>
       <td>
        As with many
        <a href="/wiki/Religious_text" title="Religious text">
         holy books
        </a>
        , the Quran has been subject to scrutiny and censorship at various points throughout history. Proposals and movements advocating outright bans of the Quran are uncommon in the West, occurring only among extremist
        <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">
         right-wing
        </a>
        circles.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">

          <span>
           [
          </span>
          100
          <span>
           ]
          </span>

        </sup>

        <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
         Russian
        </a>

        Various works
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Shen_Congwen" title="Shen Congwen">
         Shen Congwen
        </a>
        (19021988)
       </td>
       <td>
        Novels
       </td>
       <td>
        "Denounced by the Communists and Nationalists alike, Mr. Shen saw his writings banned in Taiwan, while mainland [China] publishing houses burned his books and destroyed printing plates for his novels. .... So successful was the effort to erase Mr. Shen's name from the modern literary record that few younger Chinese today recognize his name, much less the breadth of his work. Only since 1978 has the Chinese Government reissued selections of his writings, although in editions of only a few thousand copies. .... In China, his passing was unreported."

        </a>
